<h2 class="title">The Wire</h2>
<div class="headline-block-wrapper">
<div class="img-wrapper">

<li>
<a class="article-title" href="#article_0">New tunnel, premium RV section at Talladega Superspeedway on schedule despite weather</a>
<div class="article-content-wrapp" id="article_0">
<div class="article-excerpt">
<div class="text-small">
<p>Excerpt:</p>
<blockquote><p>Construction of a new oversized vehicle tunnel and premium RV infield parking section at Talladega Superspeedway is still on schedule to be completed in time for the April NASCAR race, despite large amounts of rainfall and unusual groundwater conditions underneath the track.</p>
<p>Track Chairman Grant Lynch, during a news conference Wednesday at the track, said he’s amazed the general contractor, Taylor Corporation of Oxford, has been able to keep the project on schedule.</p>
<p>“The amount of water they have pumped out of that and the extra engineering they did from the original design, basically to keep that tunnel from floating up out of the earth, was remarkable,” Lynch said.</p>
</blockquote></div>
</div>

<a class="article-title" href="#article_0">Alabama workers built 1.6M engines in 2018 to add auto horsepower</a>
<div class="article-content-wrapp" id="article_0">

<blockquote><p>Alabama’s auto workers built nearly 1.6 million engines last year, as the state industry continues to carve out a place in global markets with innovative, high-performance parts, systems and finished vehicles.</p>
<p>Last year also saw major new developments in engine manufacturing among the state’s key players, and more advanced infrastructure is on the way in the coming year.</p>
<p>Hyundai expects to complete a key addition to its engine operations in Montgomery during the first half of 2019, while Honda continues to reap the benefits of a cutting-edge Alabama engine line installed several years ago.</p>

<div class="author">
<div class="author-logo" style="background-image: url(https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/themes/techmag-child/assets/images/yellowhammernews-icon.png);"></div>
<div class="author-options">
<a class="author url fn" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/author/henry-thornton/" rel="author" title="Posts by Henry Thornton">Henry Thornton</a>
<span>9 hours ago</span>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama Dems renew call for Medicaid expansion amid federal cash infusion from stimulus bill</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Dem-medicaid-expansion-press-conference.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Henry Thornton/YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>MONTGOMERY — A bicameral group of Democrats in the Alabama Legislature has renewed calls for the state to expand the number of citizens it covers via Medicaid, arguing a financial incentive in the federal government’s recent stimulus bill will ease the financial burden of the much-debated proposal.</p>
<p>Senator Linda Coleman-Madison (D-Birmingham) hosted a press conference urging expansion on Tuesday in the Alabama State House. She was joined by Senate Minority Leader Bobby Singleton (D-Greensboro), Senators Billy Beasley (D-Clayton) and Rodger Smitherman (D-Birmingham), and Representatives Adline Clarke (D-Mobile) and Mary Moore (D-Birmingham).</p>
<p>The assembled legislators pointed out that a provision of the federal government’s recent $1.9 trillion stimulus bill would pay for 5% of the state’s annual pre-expansion Medicaid cost for two years, an estimated total of $940 million over two years. However, this incentive only applies if Alabama expands Medicaid.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            425</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">425 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-dems-renew-call-medicaid-expansion-amid-federal-cash-infusion-from-stimulus-bill/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">425 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>Singleton addressed Governor Kay Ivey directly on Tuesday, asking, “If not now, when?” with regards to Medicaid expansion.</p>
<p>The option to expand the number of people in a state who qualify for Medicaid, with the federal government covering 90% of the cost, was created by the Affordable Care Act in 2010.</p>
<p>Expansion would make Medicaid available to “most low-income adults to 138% of the federal poverty level,” in the words of the <a href="https://www.kff.org/health-reform/state-indicator/state-activity-around-expanding-medicaid-under-the-affordable-care-act/?currentTimeframe=0&amp;sortModel=%7B%22colId%22:%22Location%22,%22sort%22:%22asc%22%7D">Kaiser Family Foundation.</a> In Alabama, that amounts to an individual making up to $17,774 per year. The organization estimates that 204,000 Alabamians would become eligible for Medicaid if the state enacts expansion.</p>
<p>Calls to expand Medicaid in years past have been resisted by Republicans, who point to the high cost of the policy as a reason for expansion not being feasible. However, some Republicans have reduced what was in past years vociferous opposition to even discussing expansion.</p>
<p>When asked on Tuesday what the cost of Medicaid expansion in Alabama would be, Coleman-Madison did not reply with an exact figure. Instead, she answered that, in her view, Medicaid expansion is a moral imperative.</p>
<p><a href="https://c469e165-e7e8-4e7c-a6a5-553dd2e157f1.filesusr.com/ugd/72a465_8f37c24eeccf4e15bc6b2b97c00c3922.pdf">A report</a> from an economist at the University of Alabama in Birmingham in 2019 estimated the initial cost of expanding Medicaid at $168 million, with an average annual appropriation of around $23 million being necessary each year afterward.</p>
<p>A 2020 article from <a href="https://www.npr.org/2020/01/24/799358623/medicaid-expansion-costs-hit-new-york-and-other-states-are-watching">National Public Radio</a> showed several states that expanded Medicaid ended up enrolling more individuals than projected, requiring more state money than expected.</p>
<p>The free-market-focused Alabama Policy Institute frequently argues against expansion, pointing out that Medicaid is already one of Alabama’s largest expenditures.</p>
<p>A number of medical groups from across Alabama have continually urged the state to expand Medicaid. The incoming leader of the Medical Association of the State of Alabama, Dr. Aruna Aurora, said Tuesday that expansion would help health care providers offer more preventative care that could “get Alabama out of last place” in several health metrics.</p>
<p>Coleman-Madison expressed interest in using funds from a lottery to cover the costs of Medicaid expansion. Several bills to create a lottery have been introduced in the Alabama Legislature in the wake of a comprehensive gambling bill’s defeat earlier in March, though none of those proposals currently allocate funds for Medicaid expansion.</p>
<p>A spokesperson for Governor Ivey told multiple media outlets in recent days that the governor is “open to the discussion” on expanding Medicaid but has warned that “the problem has always been how to pay for it.”</p>
<p><em>Henry Thornton is a staff writer for Yellowhammer News. You can contact him by email: henry@yellowhammernews.com or on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/HenryThornton95">@HenryThornton95.</a></em></p>
</p>

</a>
</div>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama Gov. Kay Ivey issues state of emergency for all 67 counties ahead of severe weather threat</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/06/Alabama-Storms-Lightning-Weather.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(YHN/Pixabay)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Governor Kay Ivey has issued <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/2021-03-16-Severe-Weather-SOE.pdf">a state of emergency</a> for all 67 counties ahead of potential severe weather from Tuesday evening through Thursday morning.</p>
<p>The state of emergency goes into effect Tuesday at 6:00 p.m. CST and will allow the State of Alabama to rapidly respond to any consequences that may arise from the weather event, which Alabama Emergency Management Agency Meteorologist Jim Stefkovich <a href="https://ema.alabama.gov/2021/03/16/severe-storms-possible-today-and-tuesday-with-potential-significant-event-wednesday-into-thursday/">has called</a> “dangerous and life-threatening.”</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            145</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">145 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-gov-kay-ivey-issues-state-of-emergency-for-all-67-counties-ahead-of-severe-weather-threat/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">145 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>Ivey released a statement on Tuesday afternoon, saying, “The threat for potentially dangerous weather is rising for much of Alabama tomorrow. Out of an abundance of caution, I have issued a state of emergency for all 67 counties to ensure we are ready to act in any way needed from the state level.”</p>
<p>“Projections are showing that this will likely be a widespread event, with some of the most severe weather anticipated late Wednesday night into early Thursday morning,” she continued. “Please make preparations now in the event your area is impacted in some way. I will continue keeping a close eye on the system and encourage every Alabamian to do the same.”</p>
<p>View information about being weather prepared and aware <a href="https://www.readyalabama.gov">here.</a> The National Weather Service’s website can be accessed <a href="http://www.weather.gov">here.</a></p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama’s Robins &amp; Morton receives national honors from Associated Builders and Contractors</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Robins-Morton.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Robins &amp; Morton, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Birmingham-based Robins &amp; Morton in recent days won three 2020 National Excellence in Construction Awards in the health care and institutional categories.</p>
<p>The honors were announced at the Associated Builders and Contractors (ABC) Excellence in Construction Award Gala held March 10.</p>
<p>Projects are eligible to compete for a national excellence designation after earning award-winning status in their respective regions.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            159</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">159 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabamas-robins-morton-receives-national-honors-from-associated-builders-and-contractors/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">159 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>In addition to the three national awards, Robins &amp; Morton also took home 28 Excellence and Merit Awards from the Associated Builders and Contractors of Alabama, North Alabama, Florida East Coast, Greater Tennessee, Central Florida, South Texas and Carolinas chapters.</p>
<p>The Excellence in Construction Awards program was developed to honor innovative and high-quality merit shop construction projects. The Awards honor all construction team members, including the contractor, owner, architect and engineer. The winning projects are reportedly judged on complexity, attractiveness, unique challenges, completion time, quality, innovation, safety and cost.</p>
<p>Robins &amp; Morton is a privately-held construction firm founded in 1946. Based in the Magic City, the firm also has offices in Charlotte, Dallas, Huntsville, Miami, Nashville, Orlando and San Antonio. Robins &amp; Morton is consistently ranked as one of the top 100 contractors in the United States and one of the top 15 in the Southeast.</p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>House Judiciary Committee approves anti-riot bill on party-line vote; Democrat calls it ‘racism and white supremacy’</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Allen-Treadaway-committee.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(S. Ross/YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>MONTGOMERY — The Alabama House Judiciary Committee on Tuesday advanced HB 445, the anti-rioting bill sponsored by Rep. Allen Treadaway (R-Morris).</p>
<p>In a party-line vote, the committee gave a favorable report to the bill as <a href="http://alisondb.legislature.state.al.us/ALISON/SearchableInstruments/2021RS/PrintFiles/211817-2.pdf">substituted</a> and then <a href="http://alisondb.legislature.state.al.us/ALISON/SearchableInstruments/2021RS/PrintFiles/211941-2.pdf">amended</a> once. Reps. Chris England (D-Tuscaloosa), Merika Coleman (D-Birmingham) and Prince Chestnut (D-Selma) voted against the legislation.</p>
<p>The vote came after <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-house-judiciary-committee-sends-anti-rioting-bill-to-subcommittee/">a public hearing on the bill</a> last week; since then, Treadaway had been working with other members to help alleviate concerns that the legislation would have unintended consequences of negatively affecting First Amendment rights. The substitute was meant to address some of these issues.</p>
<p>The amendment adopted by the committee on Tuesday, proposed by Rep. Matt Simpson (R-Daphne), would change the bill’s definition of riot to the following: “The assemblage of five or more persons resulting in conduct which creates an immediate danger of damage to property or injury to persons.”</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            452</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">452 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/house-judiciary-committee-approves-anti-riot-bill-on-party-line-vote-democrat-calls-it-racism-and-white-supremacy/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">452 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>The definition of riot introduced in the bill was originally: “A tumultuous disturbance in a public place or penal institution by five or more persons assembled together and acting with a common intent which creates a grave danger of substantial damage to public, private, or other property serious bodily injury to one or more persons, or substantially obstructs a law enforcement or other government function.”</p>
<p>In a press release after the committee vote, the Montgomery-based Southern Poverty Law Center (SPLC) bashed the legislation, claiming it “would criminalize First Amendment rights to free speech and assembly.” The SPLC’s release also spoke up for the rights of local governments to defund or abolish their law enforcement agencies.</p>
<p>England — also the Alabama Democratic Party chairman — thanked Treadaway for working towards a compromise on HB 445, however, the Democrat emphasized that he still has “several issues” with the bill even in its new form. England listed the mandatory minimums imposed by the legislation as one such issue.</p>
<p>While England pledged to continue working with Treadaway on the bill, Rep. Mary Moore (D-Birmingham) took a different tact. Walking out of the committee meeting room after adjournment, she declared, “Racism and white supremacy reign.”</p>
<p>In a gaggle with reporters afterward, Treadaway responded to Moore’s allegation that the bill promotes white supremacy.</p>
<p>“That’s ridiculous,” he said. “It’s about protecting lives. And everybody is entitled to their opinion. I think if you look at the facts — I’m fact-driven, being a law enforcement officer 31 years — you look at the City of Birmingham, [the police force is] 70% African-American. These are men and women I’ve worked with — a very diverse department — for 31 years. This is not the ’60s.”</p>
<p>Treadaway underscored that peaceful protests during the civil rights era “did change the world for the good.”</p>
<p>“They also changed law enforcement for the good,” he stressed. “Are we perfect? No. But we strive to be.”</p>
<p>“We’ve got very diverse departments, very well-trained departments that are out here doing a very difficult job,” Treadaway added. “And again, we’re talking about folks — not peaceful protesters — we’re talking about when you start burning buildings, you start looting stores and assaulting police officers, these new laws kick in. And I really don’t think people disagree with that.”</p>
<p>This is not the first time this session in which a House Democrat blamed racism on a vote going against her. Rep. Juandalynn Givan (D-Birmingham) <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/house-committee-rejects-bill-allowing-localities-to-remove-historic-monuments/">tried this tactic</a> after a bill of hers was voted down by the same committee in recent weeks.</p>
<p><strong>RELATED: <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/state-rep-treadaway-on-anti-rioting-bill-this-is-not-a-race-thing-this-is-a-law-and-order-thing/">State Rep. Treadaway on anti-rioting bill: ‘This is not a race thing — This is a law and order thing’</a></strong></p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Tuberville: Democrats’ H.R. 1 trying to make ‘worst practices of pandemic-era elections mandatory in all 50 states’</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Tommy-Tuberville-floor-speech-voting.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Senator Tommy Tuberville/YouTube)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>U.S. Senator Tommy Tuberville (R-AL) on Monday <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qL6jwcwd2UM">took to the floor</a> of the United States Senate regarding H.R. 1, a bill passed by House Democrats that seeks to usurp states’ control of their own elections.</p>
<p>“Democrats have labeled the bill the For the People Act, but it really should be called ‘For the Democrats Act.’ This partisan bill represents the largest federal power grab in decades, and that’s saying a lot after Democrats rammed through a partisan $1.9 trillion stimulus bill just two weeks ago,” Alabama’s junior senator decried.</p>
<p>He outlined, “Article 1, section 4 of the Constitution grants states the authority to manage their federal election processes. H.R. 1 would take that away. The changes to our federal elections that H.R. 1 proposes should concern every single American. This bill forces a one-size-fits-all election system on our country by federally mandating how states run their elections. This phrase ‘for the people’ means allowing citizens to choose their own leaders and voting processes, not Washington dictating new rules of the game.”</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            349</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">349 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/tuberville-democrats-h-r-1-trying-to-make-worst-practices-of-pandemic-era-elections-mandatory-in-all-50-states/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">349 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>Tuberville specifically criticized that the Democrats’ legislation “would prohibit states from requiring voters to show identification, photo ID or otherwise.”</p>
<p>“Currently, 36 states have requirements where voters need to show ID to vote. Nearly 75% of states agree that it’s a good idea to confirm that you are who you say you are when you go to exercise one of the most important civic duties. But the point is states get to decide,” he explained.</p>
<p>“H.R. 1 would also make same-day voter registration mandatory in all 50 states. … Many states have already had the opportunity to consider it and adopt it, or not if they choose. But if H.R. 1 is enacted, it would overrule the laws and choices of 29 states that have already decided they don’t want such a risky provision in their voting process,” Tuberville added. “Additionally, the Democrats are using this bill to make all the worst practices of pandemic-era elections mandatory in all 50 states. Universal mail-in ballots, ballot harvesting, and drop boxes, just to name a few.”</p>
<p>He stressed, “What works for Alabama may not work for California, or Oklahoma, or vice versa. State governments know the needs of their people and communities better than bureaucrats here in Washington, D.C. They have different laws, rules, and regulations, including when it comes to voting. The same goes for the counties within each state. Jefferson County, the most populous state in Alabama, is different from Greene County, the least populous. While the state sets broad parameters, county governments are given some flexibility to run elections in the way that is accountable and responsive to their people. H.R. 1 fails to recognize the difference in our states and counties. This bill is not ‘for the people.’ It’s not ‘of the people’ or ‘by the people.’ Americans want faith and trust in their elections. They want to feel confident in a process that works. H.R. 1 injects distrust into the process, and that’s not what Americans want or need.”</p>
<p><iframe allowfullscreen="allowfullscreen" frameborder="0" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/qL6jwcwd2UM" width="560"></iframe></p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<a class="author url fn" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/author/a-message-from-alabama-realtors/" rel="author" title="Posts by A message from Alabama Realtors">A message from Alabama Realtors</a>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama’s Spring Break destinations</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Spring-Break.png');"></div>
<span class="caption">Alabama Realtors Spring Break</span>
<div class="post-content post-with-ad" data-ids="9">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Weary students and their equally winter-worn parents look forward to March and a little break from early classes, homework, projects, and deadlines. The pandemic has added stresses like virtual learning, quarantines, and limited extracurricular activities. With restrictions and safety recommendations limiting long-distance trips, Alabama has perfect Sweet Home getaways for spring break 2021. From the mountains to the Gulf of Mexico, here’s a roadmap (and a few tips for sneaking in some fun ways to learn something new) for the perfect spring break journey within a few hours’ drive.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            1144</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">1144 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabamas-spring-break-destinations-2/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">1144 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<div class="spacer-block" id="block_1331919">
<h2 class="rtedit heading-block" data-rtid="1331996">The Beaches</h2>
<div class="richtext-block hasrt" id="block_1331936">
<div class="rtedit" data-rtid="1331936" id="rt_1331936">
<p>Spring break and beaches are a perfect combination. If you’re looking for a lot of sand and some warm rays, Alabama beaches outshine their rivals. From Gulf Shores and Orange Beach to Fort Morgan and Dauphin Island, there’s a perfect spot on the sand for your chair and cooler.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="richtext-block hasrt" id="block_1331944">
<div class="rtedit" data-rtid="1331944" id="rt_1331944">
<p><img alt="" class="alignleft wp-image-157371 size-thumbnail" height="150" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Beaches-150x150.jpg" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Beaches-150x150.jpg 150w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Beaches-100x100.jpg 100w" width="150"/></p>
<p><strong>Gulf Shores </strong>and <strong>Orange Beach</strong> are the spring break meccas for beachgoers and offer all the high-rise condos, beach bars, and amusements you could want. Make a point to visit the fully restored <a href="https://lodgeatgulfstatepark.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Lodge at Gulf State Park</a>. It’s worth checking out how architects worked their magic to build an environmentally friendly resort that conserves the natural beauty of the beach.</p>
<p><em><strong>Tip</strong>: Open from 9:00 a.m. to 6:00 p.m. daily, the <a href="https://www.alapark.com/parks/gulf-state-park/interpretive-center" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Gulf State Park Interpretive Center</a> offers visitors a glimpse at how the park is preserving the environment and natural resources and what simple steps they can take to do the same when they return home.</em></p>
<p><strong>Fort Morgan </strong>is a family-friendly beach community with a good mix of beach cottages and condos located on the Gulf or Mobile Bay. Once sparsely populated and miles from restaurants, Fort Morgan now has ample beachside and bayside dining. Dog-friendly beaches allow the family’s best friend to enjoy spring break, too.</p>
<p><em><strong>Tip</strong>: Visit historic <a href="https://ahc.alabama.gov/properties/ftmorgan/ftmorgan.aspx" onclick="" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Fort Morgan</a> located at the end of Alabama Highway 180. (You can’t miss it!) Built between 1819 and 1833, the fort played a significant role in the Battle of Mobile Bay in August 1864 and was used through the Spanish-American War, World War I, and World War II. As a day trip, consider taking the <a href="https://mobilebayferry.com/" onclick="" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Mobile Bay Ferry</a> from Fort Morgan to Dauphin Island. The island is home to the <a href="https://www.disl.edu/" onclick="" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Dauphin Island Sea Lab</a> and its public aquarium.</em></p>
<h2><img alt="" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-156469" height="29" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider.png" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider.png 1200w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider-300x7.png 300w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider-1024x25.png 1024w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider-768x19.png 768w" width="1200">Point Clear</img></h2>
<p>On the eastern shore of Mobile Bay – about 45 minutes north of the Gulf beaches – sits what many call the jewel of Alabama’s resorts. The <a href="https://www.grand1847.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Grand Hotel Golf Resort and Spa</a>, built in 1847, has been named on many national lists of best resorts with its tradition of southern hospitality that entices guests to return. Swimming (there’s even a beach), fishing, biking, fine and casual dining, kids’ activities, an award-winning spa, tennis, and golf are all part of the Grand experience. Shopping and lunch in the quaint nearby city of Fairhope is a fun excursion.</p>
<p><img alt="" class="alignleft wp-image-157372 size-thumbnail" height="150" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Mobile-Bay-150x150.jpg" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Mobile-Bay-150x150.jpg 150w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Mobile-Bay-100x100.jpg 100w" width="150"/></p>
<p><em><strong>Tip</strong>: Visit the historic cemetery on the Grand Hotel property where both Union and Confederate soldiers are at rest. If you like unusual places, take a short drive to the <a href="https://www.atlasobscura.com/places/tolstoy-park-the-unusual-home-of-henry-stuart" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Hermit House</a> in Montrose, just outside of Fairhope. Listed on the National Register of Historic Places, the one-room, dome-shaped hut was built in 1928 by Henry Stuart, an Englishman, whose habits led to his title the Hermit of Montrose. The hut is located in the parking lot of an office complex at 22787 U.S. Highway 98 on property owned by Ashurst Niemeyer Real Estate.<br/>
</em></p>
<div class="hasrt heading-wrap" id="block_1332079">
<h2><img alt="" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-156469" height="29" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider.png" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider.png 1200w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider-300x7.png 300w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider-1024x25.png 1024w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider-768x19.png 768w" width="1200">City Lights</img></h2>
</div>
<div class="richtext-block hasrt" id="block_1332047">
<div class="rtedit" data-rtid="1332047" id="rt_1332047">
<p>If the spring temps at the beach are not your style, <strong>Birmingham</strong> offers a great spring break alternative with fun attractions for kids young and old. Tripping.com lists the Magic city among its <a href="https://www.tripping.com/guides/spring-break-destinations-in-alabama" rel="noopener" target="_blank">8 Best Spring Break Destinations in Alabama</a>. You’ll definitely find something to fit everyone’s idea of spring break fun at top-ranked hotels, restaurants, and entertainment venues.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="richtext-block hasrt" id="block_1332066">
<div class="rtedit" data-rtid="1332066" id="rt_1332066">
<p><img alt="" class="alignleft wp-image-157373 size-thumbnail" height="150" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Birmingham-150x150.jpg" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Birmingham-150x150.jpg 150w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Birmingham-100x100.jpg 100w" width="150"/></p>
<p>As you would expect in a big city, experiences are larger than life. Kids of all ages enjoy the <a href="https://www.mcwane.org/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">McWane Science Center</a>, <a href="https://www.birminghamzoo.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Birmingham Zoo</a>, <a href="https://topgolf.com/us/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Topgolf</a>, <a href="https://www.barbermuseum.org/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Barber Vintage Motorsports Museum</a>, and <a href="https://autobahnspeed.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Autobahn Indoor Speedway</a>. After a busy day of spring breaking, the Magic City will tempt you with internationally recognized restaurants, fun pizza joints, and brewpubs. Treat yourself to a stay at the <a href="https://www.kesslercollection.com/bohemian-mountain-brook/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Grand Bohemian Hotel</a> in nearby Mountain Brook for an out-of-the-ordinary experience. The hotel features an eclectic décor, an art gallery, a cooking school, and a spa.</p>
<p><em><strong>Tip</strong>: Work in a little spring break history lesson by visiting the <a href="https://civilrightstrail.com/attraction/birmingham-civil-rights-institute/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Birmingham Civil Rights Institute</a> – part of the U.S. Civil Rights Trail – that features a rendition of a segregated city from the 1950s, a replica of a Freedom Riders bus, and the actual door from the jail cell that held Reverend Dr. Martin Luther King, Jr.</em></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="spacer-block" id="block_1332063">
<p><img alt="" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-156469" height="29" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider.png" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider.png 1200w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider-300x7.png 300w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider-1024x25.png 1024w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Divider-768x19.png 768w" width="1200"/></p>
</div>
<div class="hasrt heading-wrap" id="block_1332033">
<h2 class="rtedit heading-block" data-rtid="1332042" id="rt_1332033">Mountain Views</h2>
</div>
<div class="richtext-block hasrt" id="block_1332108">
<div class="rtedit" data-rtid="1332108" id="rt_1332108">
<p>Alabama’s mountains are known for attracting “leaf peepers” in search of autumn color, but spring is the best time for cool-weather hikes to explore the peaks. From Monte Sano Mountain near Huntsville to Cheaha Mountain in east Alabama, you can climb every mountain your energy level will allow. Cheaha is the state’s highest point at 2,407 feet above sea level and is part of the Talladega National Forest. <a href="https://www.alapark.com/parks/cheaha-state-park" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Cheaha State Park</a> accommodations include a lodge, cabins, chalets, and campgrounds.</p>
<p><img alt="" class="alignleft wp-image-157374 size-thumbnail" height="150" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Mountains-150x150.jpg" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Mountains-150x150.jpg 150w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alabama-Realtors-Mountains-100x100.jpg 100w" width="150"/></p>
<p><strong><a href="http://www.mentonealabama.org/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Mentone</a></strong> is a popular spot for outdoor mountain fun. Located in Alabama’s northeast corner, this resort town is on the rim of Lookout Mountain. Visitors enjoy 104-foot DeSoto Falls in <a href="https://www.alapark.com/parks/desoto-state-park" rel="noopener" target="_blank">DeSoto State Park</a> where there is camping, biking, kayaking, fishing, hiking, and rappelling.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="richtext-block hasrt" id="block_1332115">
<div class="rtedit" data-rtid="1332115" id="rt_1332115">
<p>Off the beaten path near the northwest Alabama town of Phil Campbell is <a href="https://www.dismalscanyon.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Dismals Canyon</a>. Designated a National Natural Landmark in 1975, the canyon has a 1.5-mile hiking trail at its floor where you discover grottos, caverns, and waterfalls. After dark, a guided flashlight tour of the canyon reveals bioluminescent creatures called dismalites that light up the canyon walls. The Dismals Canyon also contains one of the oldest primeval forests east of the Mississippi River.</p>
<p><em><strong>Tip</strong>: If you’re driving between Birmingham and the north Alabama mountains on a pretty day, take a side trip through Blount County to see three of Alabama’s 11 remaining <a href="https://alabama.travel/road-trips/blount-county-the-covered-bridge-capital-of-alabama" rel="noopener" target="_blank">covered bridges</a>. Old Easley, Horton Mill, and Swann covered bridges are listed on the National Register of Historic Places. Yes, you can drive across the bridges, but very slowly. </em></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="richtext-block hasrt" id="block_1332131">
<div class="rtedit" data-rtid="1332131" id="rt_1332131">
<p>Whatever route you take, Alabama’s spring break destinations are sure to lead you to discover there truly is no place like Sweet Home Alabama. Enjoy the journey.</p>
</div>
</div>

</div>
</div>
</div>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>7 Things: Unemployment at the lowest rate since pandemic started, cases and hospitalizations plummet, Brooks calls out Biden administration on reckless immigration and COVID-19 policy and more …</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/7Things-Daily-New-Tuesday.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption"></span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p><strong>7. Trump makes appearance at Lynda Blanchard’s fundraiser </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>President Donald Trump made an <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-senate-candidate-lynda-blanchard-hosts-mar-a-lago-fundraiser-gets-surprise-visit-from-trump/">appearance</a> at U.S. Senate candidate Lynda Blanchard’s fundraiser event held at Mar-a-Lago in Florida. It’s been reported that Trump wasn’t scheduled to attend the event.</li>
<li>Trump was only at the event for less than a half-hour, but he did speak about Blanchard for a moment, saying, “[Y]ou’ve announced, and it’s a big story. I can say you did a great job as ambassador.”</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>6. Mobile teachers are getting a bonus </strong></p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            626</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">626 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/7-things-unemployment-at-the-lowest-rate-since-pandemic-started-cases-and-hospitalizations-plummet-brooks-calls-out-biden-administration-on-reckless-immigration-and-covid-19-policy-and-more/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">626 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<ul>
<li>Mobile County Public School System Superintendent Chresal Threadgill has <a href="https://www.al.com/news/2021/03/mobile-superintendent-pledges-1200-bonus-for-teachers.html">announced</a> that full-time employees are going to receive a $1,200 bonus. Threadgill said in a memo the district is finally “on a positive financial footing for the first time in history,” and added that the “patience” that it took “is bitter, but its fruit is sweet.”</li>
<li>Last month, there was a petition to give teachers a bonus or raise due to work conditions through the coronavirus pandemic, and Threadgill said that if they had rushed this decision, “that would have only resulted in only bare minimum bonus for some employees.” School <a href="https://news4sanantonio.com/news/local/teachers-alliance-calls-for-saisd-to-issue-retention-bonuses">systems</a> across the <a href="https://nypost.com/2021/03/15/california-schools-discuss-using-covid-money-for-teacher-bonuses/">country</a> are considering bonuses in a year after the state of education has been less than ideal.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>5.</strong> <strong>Mississippi is opening vaccine eligibility for everyone </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Mississippi Governor Tate Reeves (R) has <a href="https://www.al.com/news/2021/03/mississippi-making-all-residents-eligible-for-covid-vaccine.html">announced</a> that starting today, all residents in Mississippi will be eligible for the coronavirus vaccine. Reeves said, “Get your shot friends – and let’s get back to normal!”</li>
<li>Before today, vaccines were available for those working at schools, first responders, anyone over 50-years-old, those with underlying health conditions and health care workers. <span style="color: #222222;">By comparison, Alabama will be opening vaccine eligibility to those 55 years and older, more essential workers and those with underlying conditions on March 22.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>4. Biden tax hike coming</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">Now that the massive stimulus bill has been rammed through without a single Republican vote, the media and their Democrats are shifting their focus to a <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/biden-immigration-political-threat/2021/03/15/bee8c83c-85a9-11eb-bfdf-4d36dab83a6d_story.html">massive</a> tax hike that would target businesses and high-earners. The first such increase since 1993.</span></li>
<li>The plan includes increasing the corporate tax rate from 21% to 28%, higher rates for those earning over $400,000 annually, increasing the estate tax, higher capital gains taxes and more. The plan would delay the taxes until 2022 because they believe the economy will be recovered by then, acknowledging that this will negatively impact the economy.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>3. Brooks is calling Fauci and Biden administration out on border crisis </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>U.S. Representative Mo Brooks (R-Huntsville) and nine other Republican congressmen have come together to <a href="https://www.al.com/news/2021/03/mo-brooks-to-fauci-biden-border-crisis-allows-illegal-immigrants-to-bring-covid-to-us.html">say</a> that Dr. Anthony Fauci needs to do what he can to stop “a dangerous new foreign pipeline for COVID-19,” which is the southern border. The media want to make this <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/biden-immigration-political-threat/2021/03/15/bee8c83c-85a9-11eb-bfdf-4d36dab83a6d_story.html">about</a> the Republicans’ response to President Joe Biden’s incompetence rather than his incompetence.</li>
<li>The letter to Fauci mentions the “catch and release” policy from Biden that’s been restarted and that no one is being quarantined or tested for the coronavirus. The congressmen wrote, “Mexico now has the highest per capita COVID fatality rate in Latin America.”</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>2. Cases and hospitalizations fall to levels not seen in nearly a year </strong></p>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">Coronavirus cases and hospitalizations are finally back down to the <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/coronavirus-cases-hospitalizations-in-alabama-fall-to-levels-not-seen-since-spring-2020/">levels</a> they were in the spring of 2020. This is with an average of 375 new cases a day in the last week; on Monday there were currently 413 people hospitalized. </span></li>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">The last time Alabama had less than 400 cases per day was June 9, and the last time there were less than 500 people hospitalized was on June 6. This comes as vaccinations have continued to increase. The state plans to do away with the mask mandate on April 9.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>1. Lowest unemployment since the beginning of the pandemic </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The Alabama Department of Labor has <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabamas-unemployment-rate-fell-to-4-3-in-january-best-result-since-pandemic-began/">released</a> the January 2021 unemployment rate, showing that the state is at 4.3% unemployment, which is the lowest it’s been since the coronavirus pandemic started.</li>
<li>In January 2020, the unemployment rate was 2.7%, but Alabama Secretary of Labor Fitzgerald Washington said that “we are making progress.” He added, “More people were employed this month and fewer were unemployed, which is always good news.”</li>
</ul>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>State Sen. Chambliss on gambling vote: I requested enabling legislation, constitutional amendment be split — That did not happen, I voted ‘no’</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/Chambliss223.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Screenshot/APTV)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Last week, State Sen. Del Marsh’s (R-Anniston) comprehensive gambling proposal fell two votes short of the required three-fifths needed for a constitutional amendment, which would have laid the groundwork for a lottery, the proliferation of casino gaming and opened the opportunity for sports gambling in Alabama.</p>
<p>The outcome was a surprise to political watchers, and it left some questioning why some members opted to vote against the Marsh proposal. Among the “no” votes was State Sen. Clyde Chambliss (R-Prattville). Chambliss had previously said the bill would be <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/state-sen-chambliss-gambling-bill-the-most-transformative-piece-of-legislation-that-we-will-see-in-our-lifetime/">the “most transformative bill” in his lifetime</a>, and he echoed that during an interview that aired on Monday’s broadcast of Mobile radio’s FM Talk 106.5.</p>
<p>According to Chambliss, had the proposal been presented with the constitutional amendment and the enabling legislation split up, he might have reconsidered his vote opposing Marsh’s effort.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            438</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">438 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/state-sen-chambliss-on-gambling-vote-i-requested-enabling-legislation-constitutional-amendment-be-split-that-did-not-happen-i-voted-no/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">438 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p><iframe frameborder="0" height="300" scrolling="no" src="https://embeds.audioboom.com/posts/7823001/embed/v4" style="background-color: transparent; display: block; padding: 0; max-width: 700px;" title="Audioboom player" width="100%"></iframe></p>
<p>“In my opinion, this is the most transformative bill we will most likely see in my lifetime,” he said. “It’s going to change our state — some people will say for the better. Some people will say for the worse. But what my job is, what the people of my district hired me to do is to go and study the details, get into the weeds and really understand the long-term ramifications of the legislation. And that is what I did. In my opinion, what we need to do and needed to do is split the enabling legislation from the [constitutional amendment], address the concerns that I had, the comments that I had, and then travel together. That was my request. That did not happen, and I voted ‘no.'”</p>
<p>“If all those conditions were met, I would consider voting for it because it is a hard place to be in denying the people the right to vote on something,” Chambliss added. “But if the bill and the legislation is not in the proper form, not in the proper order, then I have no choice. That’s what I did. I don’t regret that at all. It may come back. It may not. I don’t know. But we need to get it right. We need to have very minimal information in the Constitution. All of the details or most all the details lined out in the enabling legislation — we need to track those together. We got a draft of the enabling legislation on Friday before the CA was on the floor on Tuesday. It had not been introduced.”</p>
<p>“That was my requirement, for me personally, that they travel together,” he added. “That did happen, so thus the ‘no’ vote.”</p>
<p>Chambliss described the current circumstances within the Alabama Legislature as “pent-up demand,” meaning members were eager to pass legislation that they had set out to when running for office but had not had the opportunity because of the 2020 regular session being cut short because of the COVID-19 pandemic. For that reason, he suggested consideration of a gaming proposal could be done later, perhaps during a special session, since it would not likely be on a ballot until November 2022.</p>
<p>“There is no need to rush this,” he said. “Let’s get it right. In my opinion, we just weren’t there.”</p>
<p><strong><em><a href="http://twitter.com/jeff_poor">@Jeff_Poor</a> is a graduate of Auburn University and the University of South Alabama, the editor of <a href="https://www.breitbart.com/clips">Breitbart TV</a>, a columnist for Mobile’s <a href="https://lagniappemobile.com/category/commentary/beltway/">Lagniappe Weekly</a>, and host of Mobile’s “The Jeff Poor Show” from 9 a.m.-12 p.m. <a href="http://www.fmtalk1065.com/">on FM Talk 106.5</a>.</em></strong></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>State Rep. Robertson: Better record-keeping system would ‘start us in the right direction’ for permitless ‘constitutional’ carry system</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Robertson314.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Proncey Robertson for State House)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Nationally, some states have pushed to adopt so-called “constitutional” permitless carry, which, according to proponents, would allow someone to exercise their Second Amendment rights and carry a firearm without restrictions on the state level.</p>
<p>Despite a vocal effort supporting the practice, Alabama policymakers have been resistant to adopting the policy. State Rep. Proncey Robertson (R-Mt. Hope) attributes that in part to Alabama’s substandard record-keeping system, which poses challenges to law enforcement’s ability to track individuals prohibited from possessing a firearm.</p>
<p>During an interview that aired on Huntsville radio’s WVNN, Robertson explained how he was working to improve record-keeping, in addition to offering a lifetime permit option for gun owners in Alabama.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->

<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/state-rep-robertson-better-record-keeping-system-would-start-us-in-the-right-direction-for-permitless-constitutional-carry-system/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">710 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p><iframe frameborder="0" height="300" scrolling="no" src="https://embeds.audioboom.com/posts/7820853/embed/v4" style="background-color: transparent; display: block; padding: 0; max-width: 700px;" title="Audioboom player" width="100%"></iframe></p>
<p>“I had a lot of people reaching out to me: ‘Hey, what happened to your bill for a lifetime carry option?'” he said. “With that, I did introduce that and reached out to leadership. We’ve got it now through the Public Safety and Homeland Security Committee. Hopefully, we’ll get it to the floor next week for a vote. There’s been a lot of work done with the sheriffs’ association, as well as the NRA being involved in that, [Alabama Law Enforcement Agency] — because of the way I’m doing the bill a little bit different.”</p>
<p>“Constitutional carry or permitless carry — there are a lot of states that have gone to it,” he said. “I think we’re up to 17 or 18 — something like that. Folks want to know, why aren’t we doing that in Alabama? Well, some of these other states, and this is from my background in law enforcement, have done a better job than us over the decades of really our record-keeping, if you will, of identifying who those people are who are prohibited under state or federal law to possess a firearm. So, Alabama is almost backward in the sense of relying upon who is the good guy, right — who has a permit to help us narrow down who shouldn’t have one. I don’t think we should be doing that either.”</p>
<p>The current system of permitting, he said, has a built-in failsafe of keeping a check on individuals prohibited from possessing firearms.</p>
<p>“But to do away with the requirement to have a permit would leave our officers out there on the street with no way to determine when they come across someone who is a prohibited person,” Robertson explained. “Right now, they could at least arrest that person for failure to get a permit. In other words, possession of a firearm without a permit, carrying a concealed weapon without a permit. That allows them to do the research, to dig into those old antiquated files and find out how is the person really a restricted individual and make the felon in possession charge, for instance. That takes time.”</p>
<p>The Lawerence County Republican lawmaker says he is trying to create a better record-keeping system to aid the courts with reporting to ALEA’s Criminal Justice Information Services Division (CJIS) as a way to track which individuals are prohibited from owning a firearm based on a prior criminal charge.</p>
<p>“I’m not talking about collecting information here on people who are buying pistols,” he said. “I’m talking about an information system that collects that from the courts.”</p>
<p>Robertson likened the system to the sex offender registry, linked to an individual’s driver’s license.</p>
<p>“They would know if someone is prohibited to have a firearm,” Robertson explained. “And they would be able to deal with them accordingly. The permits then become a lot less important.”</p>
<p>He noted that most gun owners have not committed a crime and should not be subject to annual background checks.</p>
<p>“Why do you have to keep going back year after year after year to get the same background check and get the same permit over and over again?” he said. “So, to at least start us in the right direction, to move us toward the possibility that we could do a permitless system — number one, we need that record-keeping bill. Number two, I am trying to help our citizens by giving them the option to purchase a one-and-done lifetime permit.”</p>
<p>Robertson explained the cost of the permit varies from county to county, which he said was determined by local legislation. However, he added his lifetime permit proposal would include a fee of $200, with the responsibility falling on sheriff departments to conduct a background check once every five years on the lifetime permit holder.</p>
<p>“I think that is a great option for our citizens, who are law-abiding, that aren’t getting in trouble for at least a year and shouldn’t be required to come back year after year after year,” he added.</p>
<p><strong><em><a href="http://twitter.com/jeff_poor">@Jeff_Poor</a> is a graduate of Auburn University and the University of South Alabama, the editor of <a href="https://www.breitbart.com/clips">Breitbart TV</a>, a columnist for Mobile’s <a href="https://lagniappemobile.com/category/commentary/beltway/">Lagniappe Weekly</a>, and host of Mobile’s “The Jeff Poor Show” from 9 a.m.-12 p.m. <a href="http://www.fmtalk1065.com/">on FM Talk 106.5</a>.</em></strong></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Montgomery Mayor Steven Reed proposing $50M in capital projects</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Steven-Reed-Montgomery-City.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(City of Montgomery/Twitter)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Mayor Steven L. Reed on Monday announced a proposal to reinvest $50 million in Montgomery capital projects, spanning neighborhoods, community centers, public safety infrastructure, public transportation and more.</p>
<p>Reed’s plan will be considered by the Montgomery City Council on Tuesday evening.</p>
<p>The funding would come via an advantageous restructuring of existing municipal debt.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            178</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">178 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/montgomery-mayor-steven-reed-proposing-50m-in-capital-projects/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">178 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en">$50 MILLION FOR MGM: Mayor <a href="https://twitter.com/stevenlouisreed?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@stevenlouisreed</a> announced plans to invest $50 million into public safety infrastructure, neighborhoods, community centers and more! Watch this quick recap. <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/anewmontgomery?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">#anewmontgomery</a> <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/ourmgm?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">#ourmgm</a> <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/montgomeryal?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">#montgomeryal</a> <a href="https://t.co/zuYHFCElp0">pic.twitter.com/zuYHFCElp0</a></p>

<p><script async="" charset="utf-8" data-rocketlazyloadscript="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script></p>
<p>The proposal would fund signature capital improvements that include a new fire station at the intersection of Court St. and W. Fairview Avenue and a new multipurpose community center that Reed pledged would “rival any space of its kind in the state, if not in the region.”</p>
<p>Other long-needed capital projects that would come to fruition as a result of Reed’s initiative include: new sanitation trucks, facility improvements to community centers, and electric vehicles to streamline efficiency and operations in the City’s public transit system.</p>
<p><a href="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Untitled-2.png"><img alt="" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-157905" height="754" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 617px) 100vw, 617px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Untitled-2.png" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Untitled-2.png 617w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Untitled-2-245x300.png 245w" width="617"/></a></p>
<p>The funding could not be used to supplement employee salaries or adjust pay scales.</p>
<p>Read more details via <a href="https://www.montgomeryadvertiser.com/story/news/2021/03/15/montgomery-expects-spend-50-m-these-improvement-projects/4701555001/">The Montgomery Advertiser</a> or <a href="https://www.wsfa.com/2021/03/15/montgomery-mayor-announce-new-development-project-plans-pm/">WSFA.</a></p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>What Alabamians need to know about the latest activity on Goat Hill — March 16, 2021</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/State-House-Session-Update-Stamp.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(State of Alabama)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>MONTGOMERY — The Alabama Legislature on Tuesday will meet for the 15th day of its 2021 regular session.</p>
<p>The completion of this day will mark the halfway point in legislative days for the session.</p>
<p><em>Here’s what you should look out for on the day:</em></p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            430</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">430 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/what-alabamians-need-to-know-about-the-latest-activity-on-goat-hill-march-16-2021/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">430 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<h4>Alabama Senate</h4>
<p>The Senate will gavel in at 3:00 p.m. on Tuesday.</p>
<p>The later-than-usual start time will accommodate Finance and Taxation Education meeting at 1:00 p.m. to consider the Education Trust Fund budget package. The proposal includes a 2% pay increase for teachers and other education employees, to match the raise proposed in the <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/house-passes-largest-ever-general-fund-budget-including-2-raise-for-state-employees-and-increase-in-mental-health-funds/">General Fund budget package</a> for state employees. A spreadsheet of the governor’s recommended ETF budget can be found <a href="http://lsa.state.al.us/PDF/Fiscal/FY2022/ETF/ETF-FY-2022-Gov-Rec.pdf">here</a>; the committee is set to consider a substitute version of the budget bill. Advancing the budget package from committee on Tuesday will enable the legislation to receive a second reading the same day, allowing it to be on the Senate floor on Thursday. Legislative leaders have said they want the budgets out of their respective chamber of origin by the legislative spring break, which is next week, so Tuesday’s committee action will keep the ETF on that timeline.</p>
<p>At 11:00 a.m. on Tuesday, Senate Democrats will hold a press conference regarding the prospect of Medicaid expansion in Alabama. The newly enacted congressional stimulus legislation has reignited the prospect of the federal government footing much of the bill for the Yellowhammer State to expand Medicaid coverage, and Democrats and several stakeholders are renewing their calls for the State of Alabama to do so.</p>
<p>Governor Kay Ivey’s spokesperson on Thursday said in a statement to Yellowhammer News, “Ensuring every Alabamian has access to quality health care is important to the governor and always has been a priority of hers. However, as she has made clear, the problem has always been how to pay for it. She is open to the discussion, but right now, we simply do not have all the facts. This is a massive (federal) package, and our Finance Department and Medicaid Agency will need thoroughly review it before we can fully weigh in on this issue.”</p>
<h3>Alabama House</h3>
<p>The House is scheduled to convene at 1:00 p.m. on Tuesday.</p>
<p>Just like the upper chamber, the House has some legislation that it wants to get out of committee for a second reading on the day so the bills can be moved on the floor on Thursday ahead of spring break.</p>
<p>This includes <a href="http://alisondb.legislature.state.al.us/ALISON/SearchableInstruments/2021RS/PrintFiles/HB445-int.pdf">HB 445,</a> which will be up in Judiciary at 11:00 a.m. on Tuesday. The anti-riot bill <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-house-judiciary-committee-sends-anti-rioting-bill-to-subcommittee/">was sent</a> to a subcommittee last week.</p>
<p>At the same time, <a href="http://alisondb.legislature.state.al.us/ALISON/SearchableInstruments/2021RS/PrintFiles/SB10-int.pdf">SB 10,</a> the Vulnerable Child Compassion and Protection Act, is set to be considered by Health.</p>
<p>Livestreams are available for certain committee rooms and both chambers <a href="http://alisondb.legislature.state.al.us/Alison/LegVideo.aspx">here.</a></p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="content-post clearfix">
<div class="author">
<div class="author-logo" style="background-image: url(https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/themes/techmag-child/assets/images/yellowhammernews-icon.png);"></div>
<div class="author-options">
<a class="author url fn" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/author/matt-wilson/" rel="author" title="Posts by Matt Wilson">Matt Wilson</a>
<span>20 hours ago</span>
</div>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>LISTEN: Actor, director Robert Davi talks upcoming film ‘Roe v. Wade’</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/LLOP-Guest-Slider-Robert-Davi.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Robert Davi/Facebook, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Robert Davi has been in over 160 films going back to 1977. His first film was with Frank Sinatra. He is a pro-life, conservative Christian who believes in speaking up for his values.</p>
<p>His latest film, “Roe v. Wade,” comes out in the next few months. It is a historical perspective of the law that changed things in America. This film is powerful because it shows the influence the media and entertainment had at the time the law was put in place and how they teamed up to manipulate the American public.</p>
<p>In this episode, we discuss the film, cancel culture, and other issues we face today as a country. Robert does a great job of sharing why we must continue to stand for the conservative values we hold dear if we want to continue having a great country going forward.</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama Senate candidate Lynda Blanchard hosts Mar-a-Lago fundraiser, gets surprise visit from Trump</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Donald-Trump-Lynda-Blanchard-Perry-Hooper.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">From left to right: Former Alabama State Rep. Perry Hooper, former U.S. Ambassador Lynda Blanchard, former President Donald J. Trump, and Montgomery businessman John Blanchard.</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>U.S. Senate candidate Lynda Blanchard on Saturday evening held a fundraiser for her Republican campaign at Mar-a-Lago, the storied Florida resort owned by former President Donald J. Trump.</p>
<p>The fundraiser was not hosted by Trump, and he was not scheduled to attend.</p>
<p>However, as evidenced by pictures from the event obtained by Yellowhammer News, Trump did indeed stop by. While the resort functions as a private membership club, Trump also maintains his primary residence at Mar-a-Lago.</p>
<p>A source who attended the event estimated that more than 50 people attended the Blanchard fundraiser, including multiple fellow former Trump ambassadors.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            258</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">258 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-senate-candidate-lynda-blanchard-hosts-mar-a-lago-fundraiser-gets-surprise-visit-from-trump/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">258 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>Blanchard served as the U.S. ambassador to Slovenia after being nominated to the post by Trump in 2018. As <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/trump-appointed-former-ambassador-lynda-blanchard-first-to-enter-alabamas-u-s-senate-race/">highlighted in</a> Blanchard’s campaign announcement video released last month, Slovenia is the home country of former first lady Melania Trump.</p>
<p>This drew a mention from Trump at Saturday’s event, which he ended up attending for about 15 minutes.</p>
<p>“[Y]ou’ve announced, and it’s a big story,” the former president remarked to Blanchard in front of the assembled crowd. “I can say you did a great job as ambassador.”</p>
<p>Referring to Blanchard and her husband, Trump continued, “Both of you were representatives of this country, and you both did a fantastic job. And I know something about Slovenia — you know that it’s a little paradise over there.”</p>
<p>He did not make an endorsement during the fundraiser.</p>
<p>As first reported by <a href="https://www.foxnews.com/politics/alabama-gop-trump-resolution-greatest-presidents-in-history">Fox News,</a> Trump at the event was also presented with a framed copy of <a href="https://www.scribd.com/document/498609678/Alabama-GOP-Resolution#from_embed">a resolution</a> passed by the Alabama Republican Party State Executive Committee last month.</p>
<p>The resolution honors Trump as “one of the greatest and most effective presidents” in American history. Former State Rep. Perry Hooper (R-Montgomery), the sponsor of the resolution, made the presentation.</p>
<p>Besides Blanchard, no other candidate has yet to announce in the 2022 race to succeed retiring U.S. Senator Richard Shelby (R-AL). Blanchard is <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/2022-cycle-officially-begins-gop-senate-candidate-lynda-blanchard-going-up-on-tv/">currently running</a> television ads during March Madness games and on Fox News Channel.</p>
<p>She and her husband were <a href="https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/donald-trump/donors-trump-inaugural-committee-got-ambassador-nominations-are-they-qualified-n990116">major donors</a> to Trump in the 2016 and 2020 cycles.</p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<a class="view-less1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-up"></i></span>

</a>
