<div class="post-title">
<h2>International conference hosted by Birmingham lauds Alabama as ‘epicenter for industrial innovation’</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Birmingham-Alabama-Frontier-Conference.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Wikicommons, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>The Frontier 2021, a groundbreaking international industrial innovation conference, is less than a month away. However, even after the event has concluded, The Frontier is set to leave an indelible mark on Alabama.</p>
<p>This year’s version of the conference will be the inaugural time that Birmingham serves as its host site. The Magic City, monikered for its legacy stemming from the industrial revolution, was <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/registration-now-open-for-industrial-tech-conference-in-birmingham/">slated</a> to first host The Frontier last spring, however the COVID-19 pandemic had other plans. Following a 12-month <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/birmingham-frontier-conference-postponed-due-to-covid-19-concerns/">postponement,</a> the conference will be presented virtually from Birmingham <a href="https://www.accelevents.com/e/TheFrontierConference2021?discount=FR21YHAM10">April 13-April 14.</a></p>
<p>The Frontier is the nation’s only conference focused on emerging technologies for all key industrial sub-sectors.</p>
<p>The conference seeks to provide “access to a network of the world’s cutting-edge thought leaders, entrepreneurs, innovators, executives, visionaries and investors to cross-pollinate ideas, rethink the future of industrials and build a nationwide industrial innovation ecosystem.”</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            596</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">596 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/international-conference-hosted-by-birmingham-lauds-alabama-as-epicenter-for-industrial-innovation/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">596 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>Hank Torbert, founder of The Frontier, told Yellowhammer News that the conference was originally drawn to the Yellowhammer State in part due to “Alabama Power’s interest and support of our goal of building an ecosystem of innovation leaders.”</p>
<p>“We view Birmingham as the heart of an industrial innovation ecosystem that has all of the major industrial sectors,” added Torbert. Those sectors include transportation, manufacturing, energy/utilities and water management, among others.</p>
<p>Since choosing Birmingham to host the annual conference, Torbert advised that The Frontier has received “amazing support” from the major stakeholders in the area’s innovation ecosystem, including Alabama Power Company, the Economic Development Partnership of Alabama, Birmingham Business Alliance, Economic Development Association of Alabama, Techstars Alabama and state and local governmental partners.</p>
<p>You can register for The Frontier 2021 <a href="https://www.accelevents.com/e/TheFrontierConference2021?discount=FR21YHAM10">here.</a></p>
<p>However, even after the event’s latest iteration has come and gone, The Frontier will be here to stay in the <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/the-southern-silicon-valley-another-national-business-publication-names-birmingham-as-a-growing-tech-hub/">“Silicon Valley of the South.”</a></p>
<p>“As the epicenter of industrial innovation, Birmingham is the ideal host city for the conference, which will go beyond a learning and networking destination but a hub for ongoing conversation,” Torbert added. “More than just an event, the Frontier is a network where leaders in industrial innovation collaborate and cultivate a dynamic ecosystem across the Southeast.“</p>
<p>According to an internal document furnished by the conference’s leadership, The Frontier is “committed to positioning Alabama as a keystone in the broader innovation and entrepreneurship economy.”</p>
<p>The conference will help increase Alabama’s visibility across the U.S. and beyond, including with angel networks, venture capitalists, universities, research organizations, incubators, other conferences and venture challenges. The Frontier refers to the state as “the epicenter for industrial innovation in the Gulf Region.”</p>
<p>Per the conference, “Alabama already has all of the raw materials of a dynamic industrial innovation ecosystem.”</p>
<p><em>Those existing assets are reportedly as follows:</em></p>
<blockquote>
<ul>
<li>Unparalleled industrials and energy sector prowess with a global reach</li>
<li>Local and State Government are focused on “enabling” Alabama’s economy</li>
<li>Strong universities and research institutions with vital engineering,</li>
<li>Strong and growing corporate base and industry diversification</li>
<li>Diverse demographics (race, income, nationality, et. al.) are a key asset</li>
</ul>
</blockquote>
<p>The Frontier, which also views itself as a community in addition to a once-per-year conference, plans on fostering entrepreneurship within and around Birmingham, as well as increasing the area’s access to capital.</p>
<p>“The Frontier will facilitate the transfer and commercialization of technology from Alabama’s research universities and federal labs into the marketplace and to assist in the creation and growth of technology-based businesses focused on innovation in the industrials and energy sectors,” The Frontier pledges. “The Frontier can serve as the hub of Alabama’s industrial innovation entrepreneurial network where start-ups find mentors, organizational assistance, facilities for daily operations, and a roadmap for success by leveraging the State’s core focus on industrials and energy.”</p>
<p>The Frontier’s key goals include the following:</p>
<blockquote>
<ul>
<li>Position Alabama for growth through accelerating efforts to sustain a knowledge-dependent, global, entrepreneurial economy driven by innovation</li>
<li>Build on and protect leading drivers of economic growth, (e.g. manufacturing, agribusiness, energy, shipping/transportation and other industrials sectors)</li>
<li>Embrace regional and economic diversity by investing in and transforming Alabama’s traditional sectors through emerging technologies</li>
<li>Create an inclusive, transformative economy that allows all of Alabama’s residents to benefit from the state’s growth and prosperity</li>
</ul>
</blockquote>
<p>“The dynamic discussions generated by The Frontier contribute to the larger, global conversation about industrial innovation and entrepreneurship,” said Greg Barker, president of the Economic Development Partnership of Alabama. “Bringing together innovation leaders from across the country to Birmingham provides tremendous opportunity for collaboration and growth in our state and region.”<a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/2021_Frontier-Information-March.pdf"></a></p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Coronavirus cases, hospitalizations in Alabama fall to levels not seen since spring 2020</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Generic-Coronavirus-1.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(PIxabay, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>The rates of new coronavirus cases and hospitalizations in Alabama have fallen to levels the state has not experienced since the late spring of 2020.</p>
<p>Alabama was averaging 375 new cases per day over the last week as of Sunday, according to <a href="https://bamatracker.com/">BamaTracker</a>, a site that collects government data on the virus. The last time the state was under the 400 case-per-day threshold was June 9, 2020.</p>
<p>Hospitals in Alabama had 413 COVID-19 patients on Monday down 20% from 516 one week ago. The state has not had less than 500 coronavirus patients since June 6, 2020.</p>
<p>The positive signs come nearly simultaneously to the state’s unfortunate surpassing of the grim <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/ivey-orders-flags-flown-at-half-staff-to-honor-10000-alabamians-dead-from-covid-19/">10,000 deaths</a> milestone.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            380</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">380 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/coronavirus-cases-hospitalizations-in-alabama-fall-to-levels-not-seen-since-spring-2020/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">380 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p><em>EDITOR’S NOTE: The Alabama Department of Health uploaded two large backlogs of positive COVID-19 tests recently — one on March 3, and another on Monday, March 15. In both cases, the preponderance of the tests was from last year.</em></p>
<p><em>This makes many recent week-to-week comparisons impossible and means the most accurate seven-day average of case data is what was reported from March 10 thru March 14. Sunday, March 14 is the day the state was averaging 375 new cases per day.</em></p>
<figure aria-describedby="caption-attachment-157879" class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_157879" style="width: 600px"><a href="https://bamatracker.com/chart/newcases" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><img alt="" class="wp-image-157879" height="302" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-cases-March-15-300x151.png" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-cases-March-15-300x151.png 300w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-cases-March-15-768x386.png 768w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-cases-March-15-270x135.png 270w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-cases-March-15.png 845w" width="600"/></a><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-157879">Clicking image opens interactive chart in new tab. (Bamatracker)</figcaption></figure>
<p>The state’s average of new cases per day has fallen 88% from its peak of 3,080 per day on January 10.</p>
<p>Notably, over the last few months, the number of total tests reported each day in Alabama has decreased by 41% from its peak on January 18.</p>
<p>New cases are those confirmed by a chemical test performed in a laboratory setting. When including “probable” cases, those indicated by rapid tests and other methods of detection, the seven-day average <a href="https://bamatracker.com/chart/newcasesprob">rises to 551</a>.</p>
<p>Past data trends have shown around 10% of coronavirus cases end up needing treatment in the hospital.</p>
<figure aria-describedby="caption-attachment-157880" class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_157880" style="width: 600px"><a href="https://bamatracker.com/chart/confirmedhospitalizations" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><img alt="" class="wp-image-157880" height="302" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-hospitalizations-March-15-300x151.png" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-hospitalizations-March-15-300x151.png 300w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-hospitalizations-March-15-768x386.png 768w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-hospitalizations-March-15-270x135.png 270w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-hospitalizations-March-15.png 845w" width="600"/></a><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-157880">Clicking image opens interactive chart in new tab. (Bamatracker)</figcaption></figure>
<p>Alabama’s COVID-19 hospitalizations have fallen 87% from the peak of 3,084 on January 11.</p>
<p>Even as the virus plummets in its total number of new cases, it remains widespread, as 62 of Alabama’s 67 counties reported a new case on Monday.</p>
<p>The state’s death toll from the virus is currently estimated to be 10,329, with 8,120 of those confirmed by health officials and another 2,209 currently listed with COVID-19 as the “probable” cause. Very few “probable” coronavirus deaths have not later been confirmed to be virus-caused.</p>
<p>The decline in cases and hospitalizations come as vaccinations have increased. Alabama had its most productive vaccination week yet on the week ending on Saturday, and has now given at least one dose of a vaccine product to 765,724 citizens as of Monday afternoon.</p>
<p>In terms of total population, Alabama has at least begun the vaccination process for roughly 16% of its citizens.</p>
<p><em>Henry Thornton is a staff writer for Yellowhammer News. You can contact him by email: henry@yellowhammernews.com or on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/HenryThornton95">@HenryThornton95.</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>No, Birmingham doesn’t need its own mask rules and no one else does either</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Birmingham-Mask-Law.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Wikicommons, Pixabay, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>America’s reliance on the mask is slowly going away.</p>
<p>Did it work?</p>
<p>Not really.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            332</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">332 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/no-birmingham-doesnt-need-its-own-mask-rules-and-no-one-else-does-either/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">332 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-dnt="true" data-width="500">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en">Finally, an honest comparison from the mainstream press.</p>
<p>The virus spread in every state. That's why we focused on hospital capacity to take care of those who needed elevated levels of care.<a href="https://t.co/xPqmABg7hp">https://t.co/xPqmABg7hp</a></p>
<p>— Governor Kristi Noem (@govkristinoem) <a href="https://twitter.com/govkristinoem/status/1371503559724953601?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">March 15, 2021</a></p></blockquote>
<p><script async="" charset="utf-8" data-rocketlazyloadscript="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script></p>
<p>So now, it looks like we’re near the end of this.</p>
<p>Alabama Governor Kay Ivey has decided in her infinite wisdom that we can end our mask-wearing on April 9. This has been met with glee and acceptance by the citizens of the state.</p>
<p>So why are some municipalities deciding that they might continue their mask orders?</p>
<p>The City of Birmingham is going to have a <a href="https://apnews.com/article/alabama-kay-ivey-birmingham-coronavirus-pandemic-local-governments-d3bf0f3ae228ae14f9fbcbbd5d5d15db">vote</a> on April 6 about extending their mask order, and, according to City Council President William Parker, it will probably pass.</p>
<p>Based on the reporting, the reasoning for this doesn’t seem all too clear.</p>
<p>If you look at Alabama’s numbers, it is clear that the health orders had no discernible impact. I don’t blame Ivey for these orders. Her administration was trying everything to stop the spread of the virus.</p>
<p>But Birmingham is not the only municipality considering this.</p>
<p>As expected, members of the media are asking elected officials what they’re going to do on April 9, implying letting the order expire is a mistake. Most of them are saying they don’t know yet, but we all know they actually know and they all know exactly what their citizens want as well.</p>
<p>Alabamians as a whole did what they were supposed to do. They socially distanced, they stayed at home, they close their businesses, they lost their jobs, they avoided their families, they changed their lives, and now we are getting vaccinated.</p>
<p>The naysayers in the media and the nobodies on social media will tell you that Alabama didn’t take this seriously and that no one was wearing masks. We all know that is a lie.</p>
<p>Any politician at any level that decides to extend a mask order on their citizens after Ivey’s order expires deserves all the anger that is going to be coming their way.</p>
<p>It is time to let Alabamians finally breathe free beginning April 9.</p>
<p><strong><em><a href="http://www.twitter.com/TheDaleJackson">Dale Jackson</a> is a contributing writer to Yellowhammer News and hosts a talk show from 7-11 AM weekdays on <a href="http://www.wvnn.com/">WVNN</a> and on <a href="https://www.talk995.com/">Talk 99.5</a> from 10AM to noon.</em></strong></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>The World Games is an even bigger deal than you think</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/Birmingham-World-Games-2022-3.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Pixabay, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content post-with-ad" data-ids="9">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>They call it The World Games for a reason.</p>
<p>With more than 3,600 athletes from over 100 countries competing in nearly three dozen sports, The World Games is an international athletic and entertainment spectacle.</p>
<p>And it is all happening right here in Alabama from July 7 through 17 during the Summer of 2022.</p>
<p>The Yellowhammer State will take center stage for the internationally televised event which has in the past been hosted by Great Britain, Japan, Germany, Finland, Poland, Netherlands and other far away places around the globe.</p>
<p>Over the course of 11 days, more than 600 medals will be awarded to competing athletes. The Games represent the highest level of competition in softball, bowling, gymnastics, martial arts, roller sports, water skiing, archery, climbing and many more sports, including the games’ first-ever para-sport: wheelchair rugby.</p>
<p>The biggest winner of all? Alabama.</p>
<p>With thousands of athletes, fans and media descending on the state, The World Games project to generate a $256 million economic impact for Alabama.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            139</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">139 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/the-world-games-is-an-even-bigger-deal-than-you-think/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">139 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>The international event will unite global fans with the Birmingham community in 25+ unique venues around the greater metropolitan area. Event locations announced to date include Birmingham Crossplex, Boutwell Auditorium, Legion Field and the new Protective Stadium.</p>
<p>The City of Birmingham won its bid to host The Games in 2015, beating out cities in Russia and Peru. This edition marks a return of The Games to the United States for the first time since the inaugural event in Santa Clara, California in 1981.</p>
<p>The World Games 2022 will be a transformational opportunity for Alabama, generating global media exposure, welcoming athletes and fans from around the world, and serving as a catalyst to position Birmingham as a host for future events.</p>
<p><a href="https://twg2022.com/sponsors/">Custom sponsorship packages are available.</a></p>
<p>To learn more about The World Games 2022 visit <a href="https://twg2022.com/">TWG2022.com</a> or find us on <a href="https://www.facebook.com/TWG2022/">Facebook</a>, <a href="https://www.instagram.com/twg2022">Instagram</a> or <a href="https://twitter.com/twg2022">Twitter.</a></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama trucking company lands on Forbes’ best employers list for fifth straight year</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/AAA-Trucking-1.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(AAA Cooper Transportation/Contributed, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Dothan-based <a href="https://www.forbes.com/companies/aaa-cooper-transportation/?list=best-midsize-employers/&amp;sh=6cd697eb4733">AAA Cooper Transportation</a> has once again been named as one of the nation’s best midsize employers by Forbes.</p>
<p>To compile <a href="https://www.forbes.com/lists/best-midsize-employers/#5cb1db25210f">the 2021 rankings,</a> Forbes partnered with market research firm Statista by surveying 50,000 Americans working for businesses with at least 1,000 employees. Participants were asked to rate their willingness to recommend their own employers to friends and family, and to nominate organizations other than their own. Afterward, the 500 top midsize and 500 top large employers were recognized in two respective lists.</p>
<p>This is the fifth consecutive year in which Forbes has published these annual rankings that AAA Cooper was honored; the list was not published last year due to the COVID-19 pandemic.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            173</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">173 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-trucking-company-lands-on-forbes-best-employers-list-for-fifth-straight-year/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">173 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>For 2021, the trucking company landed at No. 297 on the list.</p>
<p>Scott Bowers, AAA Cooper Transportation’s vice president of Human Resources and Risk Management, said in a statement, “AAA Cooper Transportation is thrilled to be on the 2021 Forbes Best Midsize Employers list. Being recognized for a 5th consecutive year reflects a commitment to creating strong relationships based on respect, trust, and decency. I am grateful to all of our team members that exhibit these values making this recognition possible.”</p>
<p>AAA Cooper is one of the 50 largest ground transportation companies in the United States, with 5,000 employees delivering innovative transportation solutions to customers across the Southeast, Southwest and Midwest.</p>
<p>Other Alabama-based companies were also honored on Forbes’ latest midsize employer list, including Huntsville’s <a href="https://www.forbes.com/companies/colsa/?list=best-midsize-employers/&amp;sh=268982081a0b">COLSA</a> (No. 17) and <a href="https://www.forbes.com/companies/blue-cross-blue-shield-of-alabama/?list=best-midsize-employers/&amp;sh=4bea2db1578f">Blue Cross and Blue Shield of Alabama</a> (No. 32).</p>
<p>As previously reported by Yellowhammer News, the University of Alabama at Birmingham (UAB) <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/uab-named-nations-best-employer-by-forbes/">was named</a> as 2021’s top large employer by Forbes.</p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>How to find your nearest COVID-19 vaccine provider in Alabama</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/COVID-Vaccine.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Unsplash, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>A searchable, online database provides the easiest way for Alabamians to find their nearest COVID-19 vaccine provider.</p>
<p>The database of providers, courtesy of the website BamaTracker, can be <a href="https://bamatracker.com/providers">accessed here</a>.</p>
<p>Instructions on how to use the database can be found below. Additionally, links to several other web portals with vaccine booking options in Alabama are below the instructions.</p>
<p>Supplies of the vaccines are still scarce. Many locations will not have an appointment available.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            348</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">348 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/how-to-find-your-nearest-covid-19-vaccine-provider-in-alabama/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">348 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<h4>How to use the searchable database</h4>
<p><a href="https://bamatracker.com/providers">Go to the database by clicking here</a>.</p>
<p>Next, type the name of the county where you live into the box next to the word “Search.”</p>
<p>The list will then display all of the vaccine providers in your county.</p>
<p>After the list of providers in the county appears, click the name of the place at which you want to try and schedule an appointment.</p>
<p>Once you’ve clicked the name of the provider, the page will display an address and the name of the county it’s in.</p>
<p>Now, click the address. It will open a new page in Google Maps.</p>
<p>That Google Maps page should have a phone number, website or both that you can use to check on appointment availability at the site you selected.</p>
<h4>Other online vaccine appointment booking options</h4>
<p>Below the <a href="https://bamatracker.com/providers">searchable database</a> on BamaTracker is a list of the CVS locations in Alabama and whether they have available appointments.</p>
<p>A web portal to make vaccine appointments at <a href="https://www.alcovidvaccine.gov/">county health departments is available here</a>.</p>
<p>Several Walmart stores in Alabama are offering coronavirus vaccines. Members of the public can <a href="https://www.walmart.com/cp/1228302">go here to try and book a vaccination at Walmart</a>.</p>
<p>An equivalent Sam’s Club portal <a href="https://www.samsclub.com/pharmacy/immunization?imzType=covid">can be found here</a>.</p>
<p>Several AFC (PriMed, Urgent Care and Family Care) clinics are offering vaccines. An interactive map that displays <a href="https://www.zocdoc.com/vaccine/search/AL?flavor=state-search">which AFC clinics have appointments can be found here</a>.</p>
<h4>Eligibility</h4>
<p>As of March 15, any citizen in Alabama age 65 or older is eligible to get vaccinated.</p>
<p>Additionally, the following categories of people can currently get the vaccine:</p>
<blockquote><p>Health care workers<br/>
Nursing home residents<br/>
First responders<br/>
Corrections officers<br/>
Food and agriculture workers<br/>
U.S. Postal Service workers<br/>
Manufacturing workers<br/>
Grocery store workers<br/>
Public transit workers<br/>
People who work in the education sector (teachers, support staff, community college and higher education)<br/>
Childcare workers<br/>
Judiciary (including but not limited to) circuit judges, district judges and district attorneys.</p></blockquote>
<p>Eligibility for the vaccines is expanding on March 22 to include anyone age 55 or older, and any person with a serious underlying health condition.</p>
<p>More information on the coming expansion of eligibility can be <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/eligibility-for-covid-19-vaccines-in-alabama-expanding-to-all-citizens-55-anyone-with-a-comorbidity/">found here</a>.</p>
<p><em>Henry Thornton is a staff writer for Yellowhammer News. You can contact him by email: henry@yellowhammernews.com or on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/HenryThornton95">@HenryThornton95.</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Carl: Crisis on the border</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Customs-Border-Patrol-Joe-Biden.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(U.S. Customs and Border Protection/Flickr, President Joe Biden/Facebook, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>President Biden’s immigration policies have created a crisis on the border he can no longer afford to ignore. Despite his administration’s unwillingness to recognize the situation on the border as a serious humanitarian crisis, federal authorities have struggled to control this situation as a massive surge of migrants attempt to enter the U.S. illegally. Just last month, over 100,000 migrants attempted to cross the border, which is more than three times the number of attempts one year prior.</p>
<p>President Biden needs to realize his campaign promises and actions since taking office have created a crisis on the border which compromises the safety of law-abiding Americans. On the campaign trail, President Biden promised to ease immigration controls and put a moratorium on deportations, signaling to asylum-seekers the likelihood of gaining entry to the United States. He has further exacerbated the problem with his proposed immigration bill offering asylum and a pathway to citizenship to most of the illegal immigrants who are already in the United States.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            267</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">267 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/carl-crisis-on-the-border/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">267 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>The crisis on our border will continue growing if President Biden does not get serious and change his course of action. During his first days in office, he chose to no longer enforce a Trump-era rule applying Title 42 of the Public Health Safety Act to minors, which allowed the temporary suspension of entry of a person “when doing so is required in the interest of public health.” He also ended the Remain in Mexico policy requiring asylum seekers to remain in Mexico while awaiting trial. These two decisions have contributed greatly to the massive influx of asylum seekers and the inhumane overcrowding at detention facilities.</p>
<p>A recent CBS report shows Border Patrol is currently dealing with a backlog of more than 4,000 unaccompanied minors, with more than 3,200 already having been held longer than the legal limit. One Customs and Border Patrol facility in Texas is now at 729% capacity and continues growing. This is unacceptable. Just this past weekend, the White House was forced to dispatch the Federal Emergency Management Agency to assist with the ever-growing surge across the border.</p>
<p>President Biden’s reckless immigration policies and his failure to enforce our many immigration laws have created an unprecedented crisis at our border. We are a nation of law and order, and we must have a strong border to protect the health, safety and security of the American citizens. It’s more important now than ever to secure the border and fix the Biden Border Crisis before it gets even further out of hand.</p>
<p><em>Jerry Carl represents Alabama’s First Congressional District. He lives in Mobile with his wife Tina. </em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Tuberville: ‘Reckless’ Biden immigration, border policies already resulting in ‘national security and humanitarian crisis’</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Tommy-Tuberville-Senate-floor-speech-border.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Senator Tommy Tuberville/YouTube)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>U.S. Senator Tommy Tuberville (R-AL) last week delivered <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EpVijVZugDI">a speech</a> on the floor of the United States Senate focused on the worsening crisis at the country’s southwest border.</p>
<p>Tuberville in his remarks discussed the impact of President Joe Biden’s unilateral policy rollbacks, cited the unsustainable numbers of migrants flooding across the border and highlighted two measures he recommends the nation should take to address the deteriorating situation.</p>
<p>This continues Tuberville’s strong advocacy for border security <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/tuberville-speaks-out-after-biden-terminates-border-wall-construction-loosens-enforcement-of-immigration-law-on-day-one/">since</a> taking office on January 3. Last month, for example, <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/tuberville-grills-bidens-dhs-secretary-on-open-border-contradictory-covid-19-policies/">he sent</a> Biden Secretary of Homeland Security Alejandro Mayorkas a letter questioning the apparent double standard pertaining to COVID testing for American citizens entering the U.S. versus migrants illegally crossing the border. Tuberville has yet to receive a response, his office noted last week.</p>
<p>“Americans back home are paying attention,” the freshman senator remarked in his nearly 13-minute floor speech. “They are watching what’s going on and seeing how it’s getting worse by the day. The saddest thing is that this was predictable and preventable. Protecting our border and cutting down illegal immigration matters to the people of Alabama and the rest of the country.”</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            567</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">

<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/tuberville-reckless-biden-immigration-border-policies-already-resulting-in-national-security-and-humanitarian-crisis/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">567 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p><iframe allowfullscreen="allowfullscreen" frameborder="0" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/EpVijVZugDI" width="560"></iframe></p>
<p>“Alabamians are law-abiding people. We play by the rules, and we expect others to follow them, too,” Tuberville said. “When people break the rules, they have to face the consequences – plain and simple. That’s how our country should operate. By law and order. Enforcing the laws on our books cannot be optional.”</p>
<p>The Lee County resident outlined that the growing security and humanitarian crisis “is a direct result of President Biden … sending a ‘come one, come all’ signal.”</p>
<p>“President Biden has put forward an immigration proposal that would completely up-end our existing immigration policy and give out American citizenship like its candy,” Tuberville explained. “But before that, he made sure to lay the groundwork with executive orders. President Biden quickly reversed many of President Trump’s most successful border control policies with a stroke of his pen, and his Secretary of Homeland Security, whose department oversees immigration policy and border security, has made it clear he’s not interested in enforcing existing laws. We’ve seen the dangerous effects of President Biden’s policies already – and it’s barely been two months.”</p>
<p>“The data shows the number of illegal immigrants trying to cross the southern border is going up during a month when historically apprehensions are low. In fact, the staggering numbers of people arrested crossing the border illegally this January is the most any January has seen in more than a decade,” he added. “President Biden decided to message to the world that our border’s open – we shouldn’t be surprised that people showed up. We all saw this coming. We all warned that reversing President Trump’s policies would lead to a national security and humanitarian crisis.”</p>
<p>Tuberville later listed two policy recommendations to address the situation.</p>
<p>“President Biden’s policies at the border are reckless,” Alabama’s junior senator commented. “The American people can see it for themselves and the data proves how bad the situation has become in such a quick time. We can and should take positive proactive concrete steps to secure our border and strengthen our national security. There are two big items to address right away.”</p>
<p>He advised, “Number one, we should maintain the migrant protections protocol program… It was successful, hugely successful. The number of apprehensions along the border went down when people realized they couldn’t just come walking into the United States. It was exactly the kind of message we want to send: our borders are not wide open. You must follow the rules. You must stay in line.”</p>
<p>“We need to continue building the wall. My constituents expect me to hammer this every day. A strong wall will help prevent illegal migrants crossing over our border between ports of entry and avoid law enforcement,” Tuberville stated.</p>
<p>He subsequently underscored that “any immigration reform proposal must include policies that strengthen our lawful immigration system and protect our nation’s borders.”</p>
<p>“So far, President Biden’s policies do neither,” Tuberville lamented.</p>
<p>“What I, and the people of Alabama, will not stand for is a refusal to enforce the laws of today,” he concluded. “It puts our country at risk and encourages migrants to seek dangerous paths to enter our country instead of the legal paths provided. Allowing illegal immigration to go unchecked fundamentally undermines the rule of law in this country. Without laws, and without borders where those laws apply, a sovereign nation ceases to exist.”</p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama’s unemployment rate fell to 4.3% in January — Best result since pandemic began</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/Unemployment-Rate-Jobs-Economy.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Pixabay, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Alabama’s seasonally adjusted unemployment rate in January was 4.3%, the lowest rate the state has enjoyed since the beginning of the coronavirus pandemic.</p>
<p>The unemployment numbers were released by the Alabama Department of Labor (ADOL) on Monday morning. The 4.3% rate is down from 4.7% in December.</p>
<p>“As we begin a new year, it’s encouraging to see our monthly unemployment rate drop, marking a new record low since the pandemic began,” said Alabama Secretary of Labor Fitzgerald Washington in a statement.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            162</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">162 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabamas-unemployment-rate-fell-to-4-3-in-january-best-result-since-pandemic-began/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">162 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>Alabama’s unemployment rate in January 2020 was 2.7%.</p>
<p>“While we are still not where we were before this year of massive change, we are making progress,” Washington noted.</p>
<figure aria-describedby="caption-attachment-157832" class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_157832" style="width: 500px"><a href="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ADOL-unemployment-map-March-2021.jpg" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><img alt="" class="wp-image-157832" height="647" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 500px) 100vw, 500px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ADOL-unemployment-map-March-2021-232x300.jpg" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ADOL-unemployment-map-March-2021-232x300.jpg 232w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ADOL-unemployment-map-March-2021-791x1024.jpg 791w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ADOL-unemployment-map-March-2021-768x994.jpg 768w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ADOL-unemployment-map-March-2021-1187x1536.jpg 1187w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ADOL-unemployment-map-March-2021-1583x2048.jpg 1583w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ADOL-unemployment-map-March-2021.jpg 1700w" width="500"/></a><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-157832">(ADOL/Contributed)</figcaption></figure>
<p>In January, there were 2,160,347 employed persons in Alabama, compared to 2,157,736 in December and 2,180,872 in January 2020.</p>
<p>Overall, without seasonal adjustments, employment decreased in January by 28,600 jobs.</p>
<p>“This happens nearly every year and is related to holiday and seasonal employment ending,” Washington explained with regards to the decrease.</p>
<p>Shelby County performed best in the state with a 2.3% unemployment rate, Blount County followed at 2.4% with Limestone and Cullman Counties tied for third at 2.5%.</p>
<p>Wilcox and Lowndes Counties performed worst in Alabama. Both had unemployment rates over 12%.</p>
<p>Washington remarked, “More people were employed this month, and fewer were unemployed, which is always good news.”</p>
<p><em>Henry Thornton is a staff writer for Yellowhammer News. You can contact him by email: henry@yellowhammernews.com or on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/HenryThornton95">@HenryThornton95.</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama’s HomTex receives FDA green light for Level 1 surgical masks — ‘Trusted made-in-America manufacturer’</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Homtex-Masks-2.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Pixabay, YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>HomTex, an Alabama-based textile manufacturer, on Monday announced that it has received FDA Emergency Use Authorization for its Level 1 Surgical masks, green lighting their entry into the U.S. governmental and medical personal protective equipment (PPE) markets.</p>
<p>HomTex, headquartered in Cullman County, has been family-owned since its founding in 1987. It is a certified minority-owned business.</p>
<p>Back when the coronavirus widely hit the United States last March, there were no American companies producing level-three medical-grade masks domestically, seriously straining the health care system and other essential sectors amid the COVID-19 pandemic.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            465</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">465 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabamas-homtex-receives-fda-green-light-for-level-1-surgical-masks-trusted-made-in-america-manufacturer/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">465 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p><a href="https://www.madeinalabama.com/2020/04/after-shift-to-face-masks-cullmans-homtex-makes-long-term-ppe-plans/">HomTex leaped into action</a> after this dire need became apparent, investing about $5 million to rapidly shift production at its core Cullman plant to begin producing PPE.</p>
<p>Almost a year after that production shift, HomTex now manufactures 3-ply disposable masks and reusable cloth masks, which it <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-company-selected-to-provide-masks-for-u-s-capitol-complex/">supplies to the U.S. Capitol Complex,</a> and soon will produce NIOSH N-95 masks at <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/homtex-getting-over-10-5m-in-cares-act-funds-to-build-ppe-manufacturing-center-in-black-belt-creating-over-300-jobs/">a new plant in Selma.</a></p>
<p>The Alabama company is well-positioned to have the largest capacity in the nation when it comes to producing 100% made-in-America masks. HomTex also has an in-state facility in Mobile, as well as Tennessee, South Carolina and North Carolina locations.</p>
<p>“We are immensely proud of all HomTex is doing to produce PPE,” stated Katie Boyd Britt, president and CEO of the Business Council of Alabama. “Receiving this critical authorization from the FDA allows them to expand their PPE offerings and to keep Americans safe. We are thrilled to be a trusted partner as they expand their operations in Selma.”</p>
<p>While HomTex’s innovation has already successfully bolstered the nation’s PPE stock to the tune of millions of masks and helped America reopen amid the pandemic, the company does not view this as a temporary endeavor. HomTex plans to stay in the PPE business long-term, helping safeguard our national security interests.</p>
<p>Jerry Wooten, CEO of HomTex, affirmed in a Monday statement, “When I say made in America, I mean every component sourced in the US and made in the US. We believe that ramping up domestic manufacturing of PPE products is a national imperative from a safety, economic, and national security perspective, and HomTex is proud to meet that challenge.”</p>
<p>While hospitals and governments have been struggling to provide safe PPE for Americans, defective and fraudulent masks, often made in China, have flooded the U.S. market.</p>
<p>Federal law enforcement has reportedly seized 10 million counterfeit N-95 masks alone. Due to emergency procurement rules put in place during the pandemic, China and other bad actors have access to the American market that otherwise would be banned. By selling defective and counterfeit masks at rock-bottom prices, fraudsters are exploiting consumers with unsafe PPE while also undermining American manufacturing.</p>
<p>“It’s time for purchasers of critical PPE – particularly federal, state, and local governments – to wake up to the fact that Chinese and foreign-made masks are cheaper, but likely defective, counterfeit, and plain-old dangerous,” Wooten advised. “It’s important to buy safe, genuine, and approved PPE from a trusted made-in-America manufacturer. We are proud to be a strategic provider to the Architect of the US Capitol which supplies masks to the US House of Representatives, the US Capitol, and the US Senate.”</p>
<p>HomTex has the capacity to produce 700 million surgical 3-ply masks and 20 million NIOSH N-95 masks annually.</p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>7 Things: Vaccine eligibility expanding, Birmingham could keep mask mandate, stimulus money hitting bank accounts and more …</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/7Things-Daily-New-Monday.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption"></span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p><strong>7. Alabama wins the SEC Basketball Championship </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The University of Alabama’s basketball team on Sunday <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-defeats-lsu-to-win-sec-tournament-we-are-a-championship-school/">won</a> the SEC Basketball Championship against Louisiana State University (LSU).</li>
<li>Alabama now moves on to the NCAA Tournament, which will officially begin on Thursday this week.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>6. Biden doesn’t want Cuomo to resign </strong></p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            580</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">580 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/7-things-vaccine-eligibility-expanding-birmingham-could-keep-mask-mandate-stimulus-money-hitting-bank-accounts-and-more/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">580 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">President Joe Biden addressed the sexual misconduct <a href="https://www.foxnews.com/politics/biden-breaks-his-silence-on-cuomo-sexual-harassment-scandal-declines-to-call-for-his-resignation">allegations</a> against New York Governor Andrew Cuomo (D), saying, “I think the investigation is underway and we should see what it brings us.”</span></li>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">While Biden barely addressed that scandal, he’s also been quiet on the issue of nursing home deaths in New York, which Cuomo is also under investigation for. Despite mounting issues, it’s still not surprising that Biden hasn’t taken a strong position on either topic.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>5. South Korea sent masks to Alabama veterans </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>A shipment of 10,000 masks was <a href="https://www.al.com/news/2021/03/south-korea-gives-alabama-veterans-homes-10000-masks-in-recognition-of-war-service.html">delivered</a> to the Alabama Department of Veterans Affairs from the South Korean government. These masks will be used at the four veterans’ homes across the state.</li>
<li>In a letter, Prime Minister Chung Sye-kyun thanked the American Korean War veterans that fought and lost their lives in the war and thanked their families. The masks are KF94, which is a “Korean filter” mask with 94% filtering efficacy.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>4. Special sessions for gambling is possible</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">The massive failure by the Alabama State Senate to get a comprehensive gambling bill through their chamber has pretty much killed any chance a bill like that has in this session, and probably any gambling bill. That doesn’t mean it might not be <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/house-majority-leader-ledbetter-gambling-issue-could-be-tackled-in-special-session-later-this-year/">tried</a> in a special session, though.</span></li>
<li>State House Majority Leader Nathaniel Ledbetter (R-Rainsville) said it is all very possible. He advised, “I wouldn’t be surprised if we didn’t see at least one or two specials. I certainly feel like one of them is coming, and who knows — the Governor could put something in the call for us to look at this gaming. I mean, it makes sense sometimes when you do that on big issues simply because there’s not so much noise around.”</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>3. Stimulus checks hit bank accounts</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Many took to social media to talk about their stimulus checks being <a href="https://www.kiro7.com/news/trending/stimulus-update-why-are-some-people-unable-access-their-covid-19-relief-checks/JTG5F6O5CBHOFGLXIFPZWX37EA/">deposited</a> into their bank <a href="https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/14/business/stimulus-payment-pending/index.html">accounts</a> while others complained that their stimulus funds were “pending,” but it is pretty clear that people want this money now and they may have to wait until midweek to get it.</li>
<li>The money is part of the $1.9 trillion stimulus bill that also includes $86 billion for <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/07/business/dealbook/bailout-pensions-stimulus.html?auth=login-google">failing</a> private pensions, bailouts for cities and states, money for <a href="https://www.edweek.org/policy-politics/concern-about-unspent-covid-19-school-aid-continues-as-congress-moves-toward-more-relief/2021/02">schools</a> that do not need more money to open up, Obamacare <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/07/us/politics/whats-in-the-stimulus-bill.html">subsidies</a> and bans on tax <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/12/us/politics/biden-stimulus-state-tax-cuts.html">cuts</a>, but all people seem to be <a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-03-14/wells-fargo-jpmorgan-face-ire-over-timing-of-stimulus-checks">concerned</a> about is their $1,400 payment.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>2. Birmingham may keep a mask mandate </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Governor Kay Ivey has previously announced that the statewide mask <a href="https://www.al.com/news/2021/03/birmingham-official-plans-vote-to-extend-mask-mandate.html">mandate</a> will end permanently on April 9, and now Birmingham City Council President William Parker has said that they will vote on extending a city mask mandate on April 6.</li>
<li>With the end of the statewide mask mandate, local governments, businesses and schools will be able to continue a mandate if they choose to. Parker said he’s “very confident” that a mask mandate will continue in Birmingham after April 9.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>1. Vaccine eligibility expanding </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The Alabama Department of Public Health <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/eligibility-for-covid-19-vaccines-in-alabama-expanding-to-all-citizens-55-anyone-with-a-comorbidity/">announced</a> that on March 22, coronavirus vaccine eligibility will open up to group 1C, which will include those who are 55 years and older, many with underlying health conditions and many other essential workers.</li>
<li>State Health Officer Dr. Scott Harris said “This is probably going to double the number of eligible people.” He did emphasize that there still aren’t enough vaccines in the state for everyone who will be eligible.</li>
</ul>
</p>
